class="infobox-data"><span style="display:none"> (<span class="bday">1997-08-26</span>) </span>August 26, 1997<span class="noprint ForceAgeToShow"> (age&#160;26)</span><sup id="cite_ref-allmusic_2-0" </div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Labels</th><td class="infobox-data"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1129693374"><div class="hlist"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Records" title="Atlantic Records">Atlantic</a></li><li>Art@War</li><li>Hi-Level</li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Formerly of</th><td class="infobox-data"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1129693374"><div class="hlist">

</div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1066479718"></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Partner</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Naomi_Osaka" title="Naomi Osaka">Naomi Osaka</a> (2019–present)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Children</th><td class="infobox-data">1</td></tr><tr style="display:none"><td colspan="2">
</td></tr></tbody></table><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Musical artist</div>
<p><b>Cordae Amari Dunston</b> (born August 26, 1997), known mononymously as <b>Cordae</b> (formerly <b>YBN Cordae</b> and <b>Entendre</b>), is an American rapper, singer, and songwriter. He gained popularity by releasing remixes of popular songs, such as "<a href="/wiki/My_Name_Is" title="My Name Is">My Name Is</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>, and "Old Niggas", which was a response to the song "<a href="/wiki/1985_(J._Cole_song)" title="1985 (J. Cole song)">1985</a>" by <a href="/wiki/J._Cole" title="J. Cole">J. Cole</a>. Videos to both remixes were uploaded to <a href="/wiki/WorldStarHipHop" title="WorldStarHipHop">WorldStarHipHop</a>'s <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> channel, which led to a positive response from both mainstream media and the online rap community.<sup id="cite_ref-ComplexEverything_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ComplexEverything-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>His debut studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lost_Boy_(album)" title="The Lost Boy (album)">The Lost Boy</a></i>, was released in 2019 to wide acclaim; it received two nominations for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Album">Best Rap Album</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Song" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Song">Best Rap Song</a> for the single "<a href="/wiki/Bad_Idea_(YBN_Cordae_song)" title="Bad Idea (YBN Cordae song)">Bad Idea</a>" at the <a href="/wiki/62nd_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="62nd Annual Grammy Awards">62nd Grammy Awards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Cordae was a member of the <a href="/wiki/YBN_(collective)" title="YBN (collective)">YBN</a> collective from 2018 until he left the group in 2020 and dropped the "YBN" from his stage name.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cordae&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Cordae was born in <a href="/wiki/North_Carolina" title="North Carolina">North Carolina</a>, then moved to <a href="/wiki/Charles_County,_Maryland" title="Charles County, Maryland">Charles County, Maryland</a>, where he was mostly raised.<sup id="cite_ref-ComplexEverything_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ComplexEverything-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-BillTables_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BillTables-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> As a young child, he took an interest in music after his father played <a href="/wiki/Classic_hip_hop" title="Classic hip hop">classic hip hop</a> artists such as <a href="/wiki/Rakim" title="Rakim">Rakim</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Big_L" title="Big L">Big L</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Talib_Kweli" title="Talib Kweli">Talib Kweli</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> He began writing raps around the age of fifteen. As he got older, he would do research on artists through YouTube, attempting to find music like his father played.<sup id="cite_ref-Open_Space:_YBN_Cordae_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Open_Space:_YBN_Cordae-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> As Dunston grew older, he became more interested in pursuing a rap career. He prioritized his studies, but often became distracted by writing lyrics. He released three mixtapes as a teenager: "Entendre" – Anxiety (2014), I'm So Anxious (2016), and I'm So Anonymous (2017).<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> He graduated from high school in 2015 and decided to go to college at <a href="/wiki/Towson_University" title="Towson University">Towson University</a>. He dropped out in 2018, explaining that college was "bigger than him" as a first-generation student, and he was mainly doing it for his mother. He moved to Los Angeles shortly afterward.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cordae&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span id="2018.E2.80.932019:_Early_beginnings.2C_record_deal.2C_and_The_Lost_Boy"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2018–2019:_Early_beginnings,_record_deal,_and_The_Lost_Boy">2018–2019: Early beginnings, record deal, and <i>The Lost Boy</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cordae&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 2018–2019: Early beginnings, record deal, and The Lost Boy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cordae began taking his rap career seriously in early 2018. When visiting Los Angeles, he hung around <a href="/wiki/YBN_Nahmir" title="YBN Nahmir">YBN Nahmir</a> and YBN Almighty Jay , whom he'd met through social media. Nahmir had reached out to Cordae after hearing a song Dunston made with his brother Simba.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Dunston is the only member of YBN who hadn't been introduced through video games. He said he already felt like a part of YBN, and so changed from "Entendre" to "YBN Cordae". He also said that Entendre had been a name that he'd wanted to change for while: "I was just always around Nahmir and shit, those were just like my brothers... And, I was thinking, yo, I need to change my shit to like, Cordae, and shit, my actual first name. I was already "YBN" without the social tag".<sup id="cite_ref-Open_Space:_YBN_Cordae_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Open_Space:_YBN_Cordae-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In May 2018, Cordae released his first single, which he called his "introduction to the world": a remix of the 1999 song "<a href="/wiki/My_Name_Is" title="My Name Is">My Name Is</a>" by <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>. He released the song along with a music video via <a href="/wiki/WorldStarHipHop" title="WorldStarHipHop">WorldStarHipHop</a> on YouTube. He then released "Old Niggas" as a response to "1985" by J. Cole, followed by the tracks "Fighting Temptations" and "<a href="/wiki/Kung_Fu_(YBN_Cordae_song)" title="Kung Fu (YBN Cordae song)">Kung Fu</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cordae made his debut live performance at the annual Rolling Loud music festival in May 2018, where he performed with YBN Nahmir and YBN Almighty Jay. He performed with the duo again for the 2018 XXL Freshman Show in New York City, after Nahmir was announced as an inductee of the yearly freshman class.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> Dunston was then announced to be joining <a href="/wiki/Juice_Wrld" title="Juice Wrld">Juice Wrld</a> on his North American WRLD Domination tour from May to September 2018, along with <a href="/wiki/Lil_Mosey" title="Lil Mosey">Lil Mosey</a> and Blake, ended up reaching 28 cities.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Soon after, it was announced that the YBN collective would make a month-long tour in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Dunston said he would release singles until his debut project was complete.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> On August 2, 2018, Nahmir and Cordae released a video for their single "Pain Away".<sup id="cite_ref-Pain_Away_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Pain_Away-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> On August 12, YBN Nahmir announced that an official YBN Mixtape featuring the trio would be released September 7, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Cordae released the music video for his single, "Scotty Pippen", on August 23, 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-Scotty_Pippen_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scotty_Pippen-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On January 28, 2019, Cordae released a music video for a new song, "Locationships", on his YouTube channel. In March, he released "<a href="/wiki/Have_Mercy_(YBN_Cordae_song)" title="Have Mercy (YBN Cordae song)">Have Mercy</a>", the lead single from his debut studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lost_Boy_(album)" title="The Lost Boy (album)">The Lost Boy</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-HaveMercy_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HaveMercy-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> He was named as one of the members of <i><a href="/wiki/XXL_(magazine)" title="XXL (magazine)">XXL's</a></i> "2019 Freshman Class" on June 20.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Cordae released "<a href="/wiki/Bad_Idea_(YBN_Cordae_song)" title="Bad Idea (YBN Cordae song)">Bad Idea</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/RNP_(song)" title="RNP (song)">RNP</a>" as the second and third singles from the album,<sup id="cite_ref-BadIdea_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BadIdea-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-RNP_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RNP-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> and finally the album itself on July 26, 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-LostBoy_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LostBoy-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The album landed YBN Cordae two nominations at the <a href="/wiki/62nd_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="62nd Annual Grammy Awards">62nd Grammy Awards</a>: <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Album">Best Rap Album</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap_Song" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap Song">Best Rap Song</a> for the single "Bad Idea".<sup id="cite_ref-:0_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> In November, YBN Cordae announced that he would be headlining "The Lost Boy in America Tour", which began in January 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-COS_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-COS-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="2020.E2.80.93present:_Disbanding_of_YBN.2C_and_From_a_Birds_Eye_View"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2020–present:_Disbanding_of_YBN,_and_From_a_Birds_Eye_View">2020–present: Disbanding of YBN, and <i>From a Birds Eye View</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cordae&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 2020–present: Disbanding of YBN, and From a Birds Eye View">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On August 6, 2020, YBN Nahmir announced on Twitter that the YBN collective had disbanded after a period of tension during which he and Cordae had stopped communicating.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Cordae subsequently dropped the YBN from his stage name and asked YBN Nahmir for his blessing of the name change.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> On August 27, Cordae released a new single, "<a href="/wiki/Gifted_(song)" title="Gifted (song)">Gifted</a>", featuring <a href="/wiki/Roddy_Ricch" title="Roddy Ricch">Roddy Ricch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Gifted_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gifted-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On April 22, 2021, Cordae released the EP <i><a href="/wiki/Just_Until..._(EP)" title="Just Until... (EP)">Just Until...</a></i> - featuring <a href="/wiki/Q-Tip_(musician)" title="Q-Tip (musician)">Q-Tip</a> and <a href="/wiki/Young_Thug" title="Young Thug">Young Thug</a>, in anticipation of his second studio album.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> On October 7, 2021, he released the single "<a href="/wiki/Super_(Cordae_song)" title="Super (Cordae song)">Super</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cordae released his second studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/From_a_Birds_Eye_View_(album)" title="From a Birds Eye View (album)">From a Birds Eye View</a>,</i> on January 14, 2022. The 14-song album features Eminem, <a href="/wiki/Stevie_Wonder" title="Stevie Wonder">Stevie Wonder</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gunna_(rapper)" title="Gunna (rapper)">Gunna</a>, and others.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cordae is featured by <a href="/wiki/NF_(rapper)" title="NF (rapper)">NF</a> in the song "<a href="/wiki/Careful_(NF_song)" class="mw-redirect" title="Careful (NF song)">Careful</a>" which is the third song of the album <i><a href="/wiki/Hope_(NF_album)" title="Hope (NF album)">Hope</a></i> released on April 7, 2023. This song reached the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> for a week and landed on position 85.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_style_and_influences">Musical style and influences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cordae&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Musical style and influences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Cordae lists <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kid_Cudi" title="Kid Cudi">Kid Cudi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>, <a href="/wiki/Capital_Steez" title="Capital Steez">Capital Steez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lil_Wayne" title="Lil Wayne">Lil Wayne</a>, <a href="/wiki/J._Cole" title="J. Cole">J. Cole</a>, <a href="/wiki/Big_L" title="Big L">Big L</a>, <a href="/wiki/Travis_Scott" title="Travis Scott">Travis Scott</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Kendrick_Lamar" title="Kendrick Lamar">Kendrick Lamar</a> as some of his biggest influences.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Shortly after the release of <i>The Lost Boy</i>, he said his five favorite rappers were <a href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nas" title="Nas">Nas</a>, <a href="/wiki/2Pac" class="mw-redirect" title="2Pac">2Pac</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Notorious_B.I.G." title="The Notorious B.I.G.">The Notorious B.I.G.</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Big_L" title="Big L">Big L</a>. He has called Nas' album <i><a href="/wiki/It_Was_Written" title="It Was Written">It Was Written</a></i> a big influence.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> He has repeatedly said that, given his musical background and understanding of old school hip-hop and what hip-hop is evolving into, he can be the key in bridging the generational gap in hip-hop.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Respect Magazine</i> opined in 2018 that Dunston was ahead of his time as a rapper. "He is a mix of the old and new school, and the deliverance and perception of his music sets himself apart from the new generation of rappers these days. We get a clear glimpse of this in his music videos for "Old N*ggas," 'My Name Is,' and 'Kung Fu,' which all have over 5 million views on YouTube. He is building a solid buzz for himself day by day, and letting the world know his bars and rhymes are ahead of his time. He has yet to drop a project proving such."<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Revolt TV said in 2018, "There's always going to be artists who go against the grain and manage to generate conversation without being mundane or routine.  Cordae is the result of perfect timing, a need for change and managing to bridge the gap between aesthetic and talent. He's the Gohan of the YBN collective, appearing docile and juvenile but displaying a 'mastery' over words that seems at odds with old-school "hip-hoppers" belief about his age group. It is yet to be seen if his talent warrants the praise he's receiving."<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cordae&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Before leaving college, Cordae worked at a local <a href="/wiki/T.G.I._Friday%27s" class="mw-redirect" title="T.G.I. Friday&#39;s">T.G.I. Friday's</a> in Maryland. He told <a href="/wiki/Adam22" title="Adam22">Adam22</a> of No Jumper that he "hated" it and that he always knew he was destined for more.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Cordae participated in a <a href="/wiki/Black_Lives_Matter" title="Black Lives Matter">Black Lives Matter</a> protest in 2016, rapping among the crowd about the struggles he faced, and the issues he'd been noticing in his community.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> In July 2020, Dunston was arrested at a <a href="/wiki/Shooting_of_Breonna_Taylor" class="mw-redirect" title="Shooting of Breonna Taylor">Breonna Taylor</a> protest in Louisville, Kentucky, along with American professional football player <a href="/wiki/Kenny_Stills" title="Kenny Stills">Kenny Stills</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> He wore a <a href="/wiki/Defund_the_police" title="Defund the police">defund the police</a> t-shirt while watching the <a href="/wiki/2020_US_Open_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_singles#Finals" title="2020 US Open – Women&#39;s singles">2020 US Open women's singles final</a>.
</p><p>He began dating tennis star <a href="/wiki/Naomi_Osaka" title="Naomi Osaka">Naomi Osaka</a> in 2019, whom he met at a <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Clippers" title="Los Angeles Clippers">Los Angeles Clippers</a> game.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> On January 11, 2023, they announced that they are expecting their first child.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On July 7, 2023, they welcomed their first child, a girl.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> On July 11, 2023, Cordae revealed the baby’s name, Shai, at a concert.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Cordae&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-upper-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-86"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-86">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"RNP" did not enter the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, but peaked at number 15 on the <a href="/wiki/Bubbling_Under_Hot_100" title="Bubbling Under Hot 100">Bubbling Under Hot 100</a> chart.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-88"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-88">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"RNP" did not enter the <i>Billboard</i> Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs, but peaked at number three on the <i>Billboard</i> <a href="/wiki/Bubbling_Under_Hot_R%26B/Hip-Hop_Singles" class="mw-redirect" title="Bubbling Under Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Singles">Bubbling Under Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Singles</a> chart.<sup id="cite_ref-BubblingR&amp;B_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BubblingR&amp;B-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-90"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-90">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Gifted" did not enter the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, but peaked at number one on the Bubbling Under Hot 100 chart.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-94"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-94">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Super" did not enter the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, but peaked at number 23 on the Bubbling Under Hot 100 chart.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-96"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-96">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Two Tens" did not enter the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, but peaked at number 25 on the Bubbling Under Hot 100 chart.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-105"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-105">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Mama / Show Love" did not enter the Hot R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs chart, but peaked at number six on the Bubbling Under R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Singles chart.<sup id="cite_ref-BubblingR&amp;B_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BubblingR&amp;B-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-107"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-107">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Today" did not enter the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, but peaked at number 11 on the <a href="/wiki/Bubbling_Under_Hot_100" title="Bubbling Under Hot 100">Bubbling Under Hot 100</a> chart.<sup id="cite_ref-Bubbling_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bubbling-106">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-108"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-108">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">"Chronicles" did not enter the <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100, but peaked at number seven on the Bubbling Under Hot 100 chart.<sup id="cite_ref-Bubbling_106-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bubbling-106">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup></span>
